</p><p>Имя поэта носят <a href="/wiki/%D0%A2%D0%B0%D1%88%D0%BA%D0%B5%D0%BD%D1%82%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D0%B3%D0%BE%D1%81%D1%83%D0%B4%D0%B0%D1%80%D1%81%D1%82%D0%B2%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%BD%D1%8B%D0%B9_%D0%BF%D0%B5%D0%B4%D0%B0%D0%B3%D0%BE%D0%B3%D0%B8%D1%87%D0%B5%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D1%83%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%B2%D0%B5%D1%80%D1%81%D0%B8%D1%82%D0%B5%D1%82_%D0%B8%D0%BC%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B8_%D0%9D%D0%B8%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BC%D0%B8" title="Ташкентский государственный педагогический университет имени Низами">Ташкентский государственный педагогический университет</a> в столице <a href="/wiki/%D0%A3%D0%B7%D0%B1%D0%B5%D0%BA%D0%B8%D1%81%D1%82%D0%B0%D0%BD" title="Узбекистан">Узбекистана</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=%D0%98%D0%BD%D1%81%D1%82%D0%B8%D1%82%D1%83%D1%82_%D0%B0%D0%B7%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B1%D0%B0%D0%B9%D0%B4%D0%B6%D0%B0%D0%BD%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B9_%D0%BA%D1%83%D0%BB%D1%8C%D1%82%D1%83%D1%80%D1%8B_%D0%B8%D0%BC%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B8_%D0%9D%D0%B8%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BC%D0%B8_%D0%93%D1%8F%D0%BD%D0%B4%D0%B6%D0%B5%D0%B2%D0%B8_(%D0%91%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%BB%D0%B8%D0%BD)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Институт азербайджанской культуры имени Низами Гянджеви (Берлин) (страница отсутствует)">Институт азербайджанской культуры</a> в <a href="/wiki/%D0%91%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%BB%D0%B8%D0%BD" title="Берлин">Берлине</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-250"><a href="#cite_note-250">[250]</a></sup>, <a href="/wiki/%D0%9D%D0%B8%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BC%D0%B8_(%D1%81%D0%B5%D0%BB%D0%BE)" title="Низами (село)">село Низами</a> в <a href="/wiki/%D0%90%D1%80%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%B0%D1%82%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B0%D1%8F_%D0%BE%D0%B1%D0%BB%D0%B0%D1%81%D1%82%D1%8C" title="Араратская область">Араратской области</a> <a href="/wiki/%D0%90%D1%80%D0%BC%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B8%D1%8F" title="Армения">Армении</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-251"><a href="#cite_note-251">[251]</a></sup> и др.
</p><p>30 сентября 2012 года в г. <a href="/wiki/%D0%93%D1%8F%D0%BD%D0%B4%D0%B6%D0%B0" title="Гянджа">Гянджа</a> был создан <a href="/wiki/%D0%9C%D0%B5%D0%B6%D0%B4%D1%83%D0%BD%D0%B0%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B4%D0%BD%D1%8B%D0%B9_%D1%86%D0%B5%D0%BD%D1%82%D1%80_%D0%9D%D0%B8%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BC%D0%B8_%D0%93%D1%8F%D0%BD%D0%B4%D0%B6%D0%B5%D0%B2%D0%B8" title="Международный центр Низами Гянджеви">Международный центр Низами Гянджеви</a>. Один из сопредседателей — директор <a href="/wiki/%D0%91%D0%B8%D0%B1%D0%BB%D0%B8%D0%BE%D1%82%D0%B5%D0%BA%D0%B0_%D0%90%D0%BB%D0%B5%D0%BA%D1%81%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%B4%D1%80%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%B0" title="Библиотека Александрина">Новой Александрийской библиотеки</a>, бывший первый вице-президент Всемирного банка <a href="/wiki/%D0%A1%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B3%D0%B5%D0%BB%D1%8C%D0%B4%D0%B8%D0%BD,_%D0%98%D1%81%D0%BC%D0%B0%D0%B8%D0%BB" title="Серагельдин, Исмаил">Исмаил Серагельдин</a>. Центр изучает наследие поэта, ценности, которые он прививал своим творчеством, ведёт просветительную работу, распространяя знания о деятельности и творчестве Низами<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-g1_252-0"><a href="#cite_note-g1-252">[252]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-g2_253-0"><a href="#cite_note-g2-253">[253]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-g3_254-0"><a href="#cite_note-g3-254">[254]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-g4_255-0"><a href="#cite_note-g4-255">[255]</a></sup>.
</p><p>13 марта 2014 г. в Государственном Эрмитаже состоялся вечер памяти о научной конференции, посвященной 800-летию Низами, проведенной Эрмитажем в блокадном Ленинграде в октябре 1941 года<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-256"><a href="#cite_note-256">[256]</a></sup>.
</p><p>16 мая 2014 года Милли Меджлис Азербайджана на пленарном заседании внес изменения в Закон Азербайджанской Республики «Об учреждении орденов и медалей Азербайджанской Республики», предусматривающие учреждение <a href="/wiki/%D0%97%D0%BE%D0%BB%D0%BE%D1%82%D0%B0%D1%8F_%D0%BC%D0%B5%D0%B4%D0%B0%D0%BB%D1%8C_%D0%B8%D0%BC%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B8_%D0%9D%D0%B8%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BC%D0%B8_%D0%93%D1%8F%D0%BD%D0%B4%D0%B6%D0%B5%D0%B2%D0%B8" title="Золотая медаль имени Низами Гянджеви">Золотой медали имени Низами Гянджеви</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-257"><a href="#cite_note-257">[257]</a></sup>.
</p><p>В январе 2021 года <a href="/wiki/%D0%9F%D1%80%D0%B5%D0%B7%D0%B8%D0%B4%D0%B5%D0%BD%D1%82_%D0%90%D0%B7%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B1%D0%B0%D0%B9%D0%B4%D0%B6%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%B0" title="Президент Азербайджана">президент Азербайджанской Республики</a> <a href="/wiki/%D0%90%D0%BB%D0%B8%D0%B5%D0%B2,_%D0%98%D0%BB%D1%8C%D1%85%D0%B0%D0%BC_%D0%93%D0%B5%D0%B9%D0%B4%D0%B0%D1%80_%D0%BE%D0%B3%D0%BB%D1%8B" title="Алиев, Ильхам Гейдар оглы">Ильхам Алиев</a> подписал распоряжение об объявлении <a href="/wiki/2021_%D0%B3%D0%BE%D0%B4" title="2021 год">2021 года</a> в Азербайджане Годом Низами Гянджеви<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-258"><a href="#cite_note-258">[258]</a></sup>.
</p><p>В сентябре 2021 года в <a href="/wiki/%D0%A5%D0%B0%D1%80%D1%8C%D0%BA%D0%BE%D0%B2" title="Харьков">Харькове</a>, <a href="/wiki/%D0%A3%D0%BA%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%B0" title="Украина">Украина</a> состоялось открытие памятника Низами Гянджеви<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-259"><a href="#cite_note-259">[259]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-260"><a href="#cite_note-260">[260]</a></sup>.
</p>

</li>
<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 275px">

</li>

<li id="cite_note-5"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-5">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text"><span class="citation"><i>K. A. Luther.</i> <span lang="en"><a class="external text" href="http://www.iranica.com/articles/atabakan-e-adarbayjan" rel="nofollow">ATĀBAKĀN-E ĀḎARBĀYJĀN</a></span> <span class="ref-info" style="cursor:help;" title="на английском языке">(англ.)</span>. <i>Encyclopedia</i>. Iranica (15 декабря 1987). Дата обращения: 2 сентября 2010. <a class="external text" href="https://www.webcitation.org/61HMDtge2?url=http://www.iranicaonline.org/articles/atabakan-e-adarbayjan" rel="nofollow">Архивировано</a> 28 августа 2011 года.</span><blockquote><p>ATĀBAKĀN-E ĀḎARBĀYJĀN, an influential family of military slave origin, also called Ildegozids, ruled parts of Arrān and Azerbaijan from about 530/1135-36 to 622/1225; as «Great Atābaks» (atābakān-e aʿẓam) of the Saljuq sultans of Persian Iraq (western Iran), they effectively controlled the sultans from 555/1160 to 587/1181; in their third phase they were again local rulers in Arrān and Azerbaijan until the territories which had not already been lost to the Georgians, were seized by Jalāl-al-dīn Ḵᵛārazmšāh in 622/1225.</p></blockquote></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-6"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-6">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text"><span class="citation"><i>K. A. Luther.</i> <span lang="en"><a class="external text" href="http://www.iranica.com/articles/atabakan-e-adarbayjan" rel="nofollow">ATĀBAKĀN-E ĀḎARBĀYJĀN</a></span> <span class="ref-info" style="cursor:help;" title="на английском языке">(англ.)</span>. <i>Encyclopedia</i>. Iranica (15 декабря 1987). Дата обращения: 2 сентября 2010. <a class="external text" href="https://www.webcitation.org/61HMDtge2?url=http://www.iranicaonline.org/articles/atabakan-e-adarbayjan" rel="nofollow">Архивировано</a> 28 августа 2011 года.</span><blockquote><p>Īldegoz… He also sought to secure his position on the edges of the declining Saljuq empire by gaining control over parts of Azerbaijan; he probably gained clear control over it only after the death of Masʿūd’s last favorite, Ḵāṣṣ Beg Arslān b. Palangarī in 548/1153, who had been given a position in that area as well. </p></blockquote></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-7"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-7">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text"><span class="citation no-wikidata" data-wikidata-property-id="P1343"><i><a href="/wiki/%D0%91%D0%B0%D1%80%D1%82%D0%BE%D0%BB%D1%8C%D0%B4,_%D0%92%D0%B0%D1%81%D0%B8%D0%BB%D0%B8%D0%B9_%D0%92%D0%BB%D0%B0%D0%B4%D0%B8%D0%BC%D0%B8%D1%80%D0%BE%D0%B2%D0%B8%D1%87" title="Бартольд, Василий Владимирович">Barthold, W.</a>, <a href="/wiki/%D0%91%D0%BE%D1%81%D1%83%D0%BE%D1%80%D1%82,_%D0%9A%D0%BB%D0%B8%D1%84%D1%84%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%B4_%D0%AD%D0%B4%D0%BC%D1%83%D0%BD%D0%B4" title="Босуорт, Клиффорд Эдмунд">C. E. Bosworth</a>.</i> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Encyclopaedia_of_Islam" title="Encyclopaedia of Islam">Encyclopaedia of Islam</a> — Shirwan Shāh / P. Bearman, <a href="/wiki/%D0%91%D1%8C%D1%8F%D0%BD%D0%BA%D0%B8,_%D0%A2%D1%8C%D0%B5%D1%80%D1%80%D0%B8" title="Бьянки, Тьерри">Th. Bianquis</a>, C.E. Bosworth, E. van Donzel and W.P. Heinrichs. — <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brill_Publishers" title="Brill Publishers">Brill</a>, 1997. — Т. 9. — С. 488.</span>
<blockquote><p>We can also discern the <b>progressive Persianisation of this originally Arab family</b> (a process parallel to and contemporary with that of the Kurdicisation of the Rawwadids [q.v.] in Adharbaydjan). After the <b>Shah Yazid b. Ahmad</b> (381—418/991-1028), Arab names give way to Persian ones like Manuchihr, Kubadh, Faridun, etc., very likely as a reflection of marriage links with local families, and possibly with that of the ancient rulers in Shabaran, the former capital, and the Yazidids now began to claim a nasab going back to Bahrain Gur or to Khusraw Anushirwan.</p></blockquote></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-8"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-8">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text"><span class="citation no-wikidata" data-wikidata-property-id="P1343"><i><a href="/wiki/%D0%93%D1%80%D1%83%D1%81%D1%81%D0%B5,_%D0%A0%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B5" title="Груссе, Рене">Grousset, Rene</a>.</i> <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=CHzGvqRbV_IC&amp;dq=Grousset,+Rene+The+Empire+of+the+Steppes&amp;source=gbs_navlinks_s" rel="nofollow">The Empire of the Steppes: A History of Central Asia</a>. — <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rutgers_University_Press" title="Rutgers University Press">Rutgers University Press</a>, 1970. — С. 161—164. — 718 с. — <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/%D0%A1%D0%BB%D1%83%D0%B6%D0%B5%D0%B1%D0%BD%D0%B0%D1%8F:%D0%98%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BE%D1%87%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%B8_%D0%BA%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%B3/0813513049">ISBN 0813513049</a>. — <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/%D0%A1%D0%BB%D1%83%D0%B6%D0%B5%D0%B1%D0%BD%D0%B0%D1%8F:%D0%98%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BE%D1%87%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%B8_%D0%BA%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%B3/9780813513041">ISBN 9780813513041</a>.</span><blockquote><p>«It is to be noted that the Seljuks, those Turkomans who became sultans of Persia, did not Turkify Persia — no doubt because they did not wish to do so. On the contrary, it was they who <b>voluntarily became Persians and who, in the manner of the great old Sassanid kings, strove to protect the Iranian populations from the plundering of Ghuzz bands and save Iranian culture from the Turkoman menace</b>.»</p></blockquote></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-9"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-9">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text">Peter J. Chelkowski, «Mirror of the Invisible World». — New York: Metropolitan Museum of Art, 1975, P.2</span>

<li id="cite_note-Blois1-10"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">↑ <a href="#cite_ref-Blois1_10-0"><sup><i><b>1</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Blois1_10-1"><sup><i><b>2</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Blois1_10-2"><sup><i><b>3</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Blois1_10-3"><sup><i><b>4</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Blois1_10-4"><sup><i><b>5</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">
<span class="citation no-wikidata" data-wikidata-property-id="P1343"><i>Francois De Blois.</i> <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=UeMOAAAAQAAJ&amp;dq=Persian+Literature+-+A+Bio+Bibliographical+Survey:+Volume+V+Poetry+of+the+Pre-Mongol+Period%22&amp;source=gbs_navlinks_s" rel="nofollow">Persian Literature — A Biobibliographical Survey: Volume V Poetry of the Pre-Mongol Period</a> / Francois De Blois. — <a href="/wiki/Routledge" title="Routledge">Routledge</a>, 2004. — Т. V. — С. 363. — 544 с. — <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/%D0%A1%D0%BB%D1%83%D0%B6%D0%B5%D0%B1%D0%BD%D0%B0%D1%8F:%D0%98%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BE%D1%87%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%B8_%D0%BA%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%B3/0947593470">ISBN 0947593470</a>. — <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/%D0%A1%D0%BB%D1%83%D0%B6%D0%B5%D0%B1%D0%BD%D0%B0%D1%8F:%D0%98%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BE%D1%87%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%B8_%D0%BA%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%B3/9780947593476">ISBN 9780947593476</a>.</span>
<blockquote><p>Nizami Ganja’i, whose personal name was Ilyas, is the most celebrated native poet of the Persians after Firdausi… His nisbah designates him as a native of Ganja (Elizavetpol, Kirovabad) in Azerbaijan, then still a country with an Iranian population, and he spent the whole of his life in Transcaucasia; the verse in some of his poetic works which makes him a native of the hinterland of Qom is a spurious interpolation.</p></blockquote></span>
</li>

<li id="cite_note-14"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-14">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text"><span class="citation"><span lang="und"><a class="external text" href="http://www.iranica.com/articles/nozhat-al-majales" rel="nofollow">NOZHAT AL-MAJĀLES</a></span><span class="hidden-ref" style="display:none;">  <small class="ref-info" style="cursor:help;" title="на неопределённом языке">(неопр.)</small></span>. <a href="/wiki/Encyclop%C3%A6dia_Iranica" title="Encyclopædia Iranica">Encyclopædia Iranica</a>. <li id="cite_note-17"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-17">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text"><span class="citation"><i>Ḥamd-Allāh Mustawfī of Qazwīn.</i> <span lang="en"><a class="external text" href="https://www.webcitation.org/61HMFWInK?url=http://persian.packhum.org/persian/main?url=pf%3Ffile%3D16301012&amp;ct=11" rel="nofollow">The Geographical Part of the NUZHAT-AL-QULŪB</a></span> <span class="ref-info" style="cursor:help;" title="на английском языке">(англ.)</span>. <i>Persian Literature in Translation</i>. <li id="cite_note-18"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-18">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text">
<span class="citation no-wikidata" data-wikidata-property-id="P1343"><i>Peter Chelkowski.</i> <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=I1iIQwAACAAJ&amp;dq=Peter+Chelkowski,+Literature+in+Pre-Safavid&amp;hl=en&amp;ei=hyt4Te7uOoWg8QPo7vyfDA&amp;sa=X&amp;oi=book_result&amp;ct=result&amp;resnum=1&amp;ved=0CCcQ6AEwAA" rel="nofollow">Literature in Pre-Safavid Isfahan</a>. — <a href="/wiki/Taylor_%26_Francis" title="Taylor &amp; Francis">Taylor &amp; Francis</a>, Ltd. on behalf of International Society for Iranian Studies, 1974. — Т. 7. — С. 112—131.</span><blockquote><p>«The three main literary styles which follow each other consecutively are known as: <b>Khurasani, Iraqi, and Hindi</b>. The time spans of each style are equally flexible. Within these broad geographical divisions we then come across certain „literary schools“ which reflect regional peculiarities and idiosyncrasies and are identified with smaller entities like provinces or towns. For example, there are: <i>the Azerbayjani school, the Tabriz school, or the Shirvan school</i>.»</p></blockquote></span>

<li id="cite_note-20"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-20">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text"><span class="citation no-wikidata" data-wikidata-property-id="P1343"><i>Rypka, Jan.</i> <span data-wikidata-qualifier-id="P248">Poets and Prose Writers of the Late Saljuq and Mongol Periods</span> // The Cambridge History of Iran. — January 1968. — Т. 5 — The Saljuq and Mongol Periods. — С. 578.</span><blockquote><p><b>Hakim Jamal al-din Abu Muhammad Ilyas b. <li id="cite_note-Oxford-1-21"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-Oxford-1_21-0">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text"><span class="citation no-wikidata" data-wikidata-property-id="P1343"><i>Niẓāmī Ganjavī,.</i> <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=8vxjAAAAMAAJ&amp;q=Julie+Scott+Meisami+%22The+Haft+Paykar:+A+Medieval+Persian+Romance&amp;dq=Julie+Scott+Meisami+%22The+Haft+Paykar:+A+Medieval+Persian+Romance&amp;hl=en&amp;ei=yjZ4TbXAFsa48gOH7K2gDA&amp;sa=X&amp;oi=book_result&amp;ct=result&amp;resnum=1&amp;ved=0CCcQ6AEwAA" rel="nofollow">The haft paykar: a medieval Persian romance</a> <small class="ref-info" style="cursor:help;" title="на английском языке">(англ.)</small> / Julie Scott Meisami. — Oxford: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oxford_University_Press" title="Oxford University Press">Oxford University Press</a>, 1995. — 307 p. — <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/%D0%A1%D0%BB%D1%83%D0%B6%D0%B5%D0%B1%D0%BD%D0%B0%D1%8F:%D0%98%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BE%D1%87%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%B8_%D0%BA%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%B3/0192831844">ISBN 0-19-283184-4</a>.</span><blockquote><p>«Abû Muhammad Ilyas ibn Yusuf ibn Zaki Mu’ayyad, known by his pen-name of Nizami… He lived in an age of both political instability and intense intellectual activity, which his poems reflect; but <b>little is known about his life, his relations with his patrons, or the precise dates of his works, as the accounts of later biographers are colored by the many legends built up around the poet.</b>»</p></blockquote></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-22"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-22">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text"><span class="citation no-wikidata" data-wikidata-property-id="P1343"><i>Julie Scott Meisami.</i> <a class="external text" href="https://archive.org/details/haftpaykarmediev00niza" rel="nofollow">The Haft Paykar: A Medieval Persian Romance</a>. — Oxford University, 1995. — (Oxford World's Classics). — <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/%D0%A1%D0%BB%D1%83%D0%B6%D0%B5%D0%B1%D0%BD%D0%B0%D1%8F:%D0%98%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BE%D1%87%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%B8_%D0%BA%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%B3/0192831844">ISBN 0-19-283184-4</a>.</span><blockquote><p>«Abû Muhammad Ilyas ibn Yusuf ibn Zaki Mu’ayyad, known by his pen-name of Nizami, was born around 1141 in Ganja, the capital of Arran in Transcaucasian Azerbaijan, where he remained until his death in about 1209.»</p></blockquote></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-23"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-23">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text"><span class="citation no-wikidata" data-wikidata-property-id="P1343"><i>Abdolhossein Zarrinkoob.</i> <span data-wikidata-qualifier-id="P248">Nizami, a life-long quest for a utopia</span> // Colloquio sul poeta persiano Nizami e la leggenda iranica di Alessandro magno (ROMA, 25-26 MARZO 1975) / G. Bardi. — Roma: <a href="/wiki/%D0%9D%D0%B0%D1%86%D0%B8%D0%BE%D0%BD%D0%B0%D0%BB%D1%8C%D0%BD%D0%B0%D1%8F_%D0%B0%D0%BA%D0%B0%D0%B4%D0%B5%D0%BC%D0%B8%D1%8F_%D0%B4%D0%B5%D0%B8_%D0%9B%D0%B8%D0%BD%D1%87%D0%B5%D0%B8" title="Национальная академия деи Линчеи">deH'Accademia Nazionale dei Lincei</a>, 1977. — P. 7.</span><blockquote><p>The generous gifts of these royal patrons, which included a Turkish slave-maid with one or two pieces of land, offered a good opportunity for the poet to work on his poetical craft with the patience of a skillful embroiderer. In fact, some writers of Tadhkiras have stated(4) that embroidering was the inherited profession of the poet’s family and that, he himself had renounced it for the sake of poetry, although there is nothing in the poet’s work that might assure us of this point. … But in all these facts, there is nothing to assure us about the poet’s craft.</p></blockquote></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-Oxford-2-24"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-Oxford-2_24-0">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text"><span class="citation no-wikidata" data-wikidata-property-id="P1343"><i>Julie Scott Meisami.</i> <a class="external text" href="https://archive.org/details/haftpaykarmediev00niza" rel="nofollow">The Haft Paykar: A Medieval Persian Romance</a>. — Oxford University, 1995. — (Oxford World's Classics). — <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/%D0%A1%D0%BB%D1%83%D0%B6%D0%B5%D0%B1%D0%BD%D0%B0%D1%8F:%D0%98%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BE%D1%87%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%B8_%D0%BA%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%B3/0192831844">ISBN 0-19-283184-4</a>.</span><blockquote><p>«Abû Muhammad Ilyas ibn Yusuf ibn Zaki Mu’ayyad, known by his pen-name of Nizami, was born around 1141 in Ganja, the capital of Arran in Transcaucasian Azerbaijan, where he remained until his death in about 1209. His father, who had migrated to Ganja from Qom in north central Iran, may have been a civil servant; his mother was a daughter of a Kurdish chieftain; having lost both parents early in his life, Nizami was brought up by an uncle. He was married three times, and in his poems laments the death of each of his wives, as well as proferring advice to his son Muhammad. He lived in an age of both political instability and intense intellectual activity, which his poems reflect; but little is known about his life, his relations with his patrons, or the precise dates of his works, as the accounts of later biographers are colored by the many legends built up around the poet.»</p></blockquote></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-25"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-25">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text"><span class="citation no-wikidata" data-wikidata-property-id="P1343"><i><a href="/wiki/%D0%A0%D1%8B%D0%BF%D0%BA%D0%B0,_%D0%AF%D0%BD" title="Рыпка, Ян">Rypka, Jan</a>, "Poets and Prose Writers of the Late Saljuq and Mongol Periods".</i> <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=16yHq5v3QZAC&amp;dq=the+cambridge+history+of+iran&amp;source=gbs_navlinks_s" rel="nofollow">The Cambridge History of Iran</a> / William Bayne Fisher, Ilya Gershevitch, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ehsan_Yarshater" title="Ehsan Yarshater">Ehsan Yarshater</a>. — Cambridge: Cambridge University Press, 1993. — Т. 5 - The Saljuq and Mongol Periods. — С. 578. — 771 с. — <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/%D0%A1%D0%BB%D1%83%D0%B6%D0%B5%D0%B1%D0%BD%D0%B0%D1%8F:%D0%98%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BE%D1%87%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%B8_%D0%BA%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%B3/052106936X">ISBN 052106936X</a>, 9780521069366.</span><blockquote><p>As the scene of the greatest flowering of the panegyrical qasida, southern Caucasia occupies a prominent place in New Persian literary history. But this region also gave to the world Persia’s finest creator of romantic epics. <b>Hakim Jamal al-din Abu Muhammad Ilyas b. Yusuf b. Zaki b. Mu’ayyad Nizami</b> a native of Ganja in Azarbaijan, is an unrivaled master of thoughts and words, a poet whose freshness and vigor all the succeeding centuries have been unable to dull.</p></blockquote></span>
</li>

<li id="cite_note-35"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-35">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text"><span class="citation"><span lang="en"><a class="external text" href="http://www.britannica.com/EBchecked/topic/413374/Nezami" rel="nofollow">Nezami</a></span> <span class="ref-info" style="cursor:help;" title="на английском языке">(англ.)</span>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Encyclop%C3%A6dia_Britannica" title="Encyclopædia Britannica">Encyclopædia Britannica</a>. Дата обращения: 8 февраля 2011. <a class="external text" href="https://www.webcitation.org/61HMHDXyC?url=http://www.britannica.com/EBchecked/topic/413374/Nezami" rel="nofollow">Архивировано</a> 28 августа 2011 года.</span><blockquote><p>Neẓāmī, in full Elyās Yūsof Neẓāmī Ganjavī, Neẓāmī also spelled Niẓāmī (b. c. 1141, <b>Ganja, Seljuq empire</b> [now Ganca, Azerbaijan]—d. 1209, Ganja), greatest romantic epic poet in Persian literature, who brought a colloquial and realistic style to the Persian epic.</p></blockquote></span>

Эд. Босворт</a>, E. van Donzel and W.P. Heinrichs (ed.). <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Encyclopaedia_of_Islam" title="Encyclopaedia of Islam">Энциклопедия ислама</a></i>. Brill Academic Publishers. ISSN 15-73-3912.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=bookitem&amp;rft.atitle=Iskandar+Nama&amp;rft.btitle=%D0%AD%D0%BD%D1%86%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%BB%D0%BE%D0%BF%D0%B5%D0%B4%D0%B8%D1%8F+%D0%B8%D1%81%D0%BB%D0%B0%D0%BC%D0%B0&amp;rft.pub=Brill+Academic+Publishers&amp;rft.au=Abel%2C+A.&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fru.wikipedia.org%3A%D0%9D%D0%B8%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BC%D0%B8+%D0%93%D1%8F%D0%BD%D0%B4%D0%B6%D0%B5%D0%B2%D0%B8"></span><span class="cs1-maint citation-comment"><code class="cs1-code">{{<a href="/wiki/%D0%A8%D0%B0%D0%B1%D0%BB%D0%BE%D0%BD:Cite_encyclopedia" title="Шаблон:Cite encyclopedia">cite encyclopedia</a>}}</code>:  Википедия:Обслуживание CS1 (множественные имена: editors list) (<a href="/wiki/%D0%9A%D0%B0%D1%82%D0%B5%D0%B3%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%B8%D1%8F:%D0%92%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%BF%D0%B5%D0%B4%D0%B8%D1%8F:%D0%9E%D0%B1%D1%81%D0%BB%D1%83%D0%B6%D0%B8%D0%B2%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%B5_CS1_(%D0%BC%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%B6%D0%B5%D1%81%D1%82%D0%B2%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%BD%D1%8B%D0%B5_%D0%B8%D0%BC%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B0:_editors_list)" title="Категория:Википедия:Обслуживание CS1 (множественные имена: editors list)">ссылка</a>)</span><blockquote><p>"As a learned Iranian poet, Niẓami, who demonstrates his eclecticism in the information he gives (he says, «I have taken from everything just what suited me and I have borrowed from recent histories, Christian, Pahlavi and Jewish … and of them I have made a whole»), locates the story of his hero principally in Iran.</p></blockquote></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-Subtelny,_Maria-48"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">↑ <a href="#cite_ref-Subtelny,_Maria_48-0"><sup><i><b>1</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Subtelny,_Maria_48-1"><sup><i><b>2</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><span class="citation no-wikidata" data-wikidata-property-id="P1343"><i>Subtelny, Maria.</i> <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=dmclFThar_UC&amp;source=gbs_navlinks_s" rel="nofollow">Visionary Rose: Metaphorical Application of Horticultural Practice in Persian Culture, «Botanical progress, horticultural information and cultural changes»</a> / Michel Conan and W. John Kress. — USA: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dumbarton_Oaks" title="Dumbarton Oaks">Dumbarton Oaks</a>, 2007. — Т. 2004. — С. 12. — 278 с. — <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/%D0%A1%D0%BB%D1%83%D0%B6%D0%B5%D0%B1%D0%BD%D0%B0%D1%8F:%D0%98%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BE%D1%87%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%B8_%D0%BA%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%B3/0884023273">ISBN 0884023273</a>, 9780884023272.</span><blockquote><p>In a highly evocative tale he relates in the Makhzan al-Asrar («Treasury of Secrets»), the twelfth-century Persian poet, Nizami whose oeuvre is an acknowledged repository of Iranian myths and legends, illustrates the way in which the rose was perceived in the Medieval Persian imagination.</p></blockquote></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-Oxford-49"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-Oxford_49-0">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text"><span class="citation no-wikidata" data-wikidata-property-id="P1343"><i>Julie Scott Meisami.</i> <a class="external text" href="https://archive.org/details/haftpaykarmediev00niza" rel="nofollow">The Haft Paykar: A Medieval Persian Romance</a>. — Oxford University, 1995. — (Oxford World's Classics). — <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/%D0%A1%D0%BB%D1%83%D0%B6%D0%B5%D0%B1%D0%BD%D0%B0%D1%8F:%D0%98%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BE%D1%87%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%B8_%D0%BA%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%B3/0192831844">ISBN 0-19-283184-4</a>.</span></span>
</li>

<li id="cite_note-51"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-51">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation encyclopaedia cs1" id="CITEREFChelkowski,_P.">Chelkowski, P. <li id="cite_note-52"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-52">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text"><span class="citation no-wikidata" data-wikidata-property-id="P1343"><i>Seyyed Hossein Nasr, Mehdi Amin Razavi.</i> <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=rXDSeOhHihcC&amp;dq=nasr+razavi+nizami&amp;source=gbs_navlinks_s" rel="nofollow">The Islamic intellectual tradition in Persia»</a> / Mehdi Amin Razavi. — annotated edition. — Routledge, 1996. — С. 187. — 375 с. — <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/%D0%A1%D0%BB%D1%83%D0%B6%D0%B5%D0%B1%D0%BD%D0%B0%D1%8F:%D0%98%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BE%D1%87%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%B8_%D0%BA%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%B3/0700703144">ISBN 0700703144</a>. — <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/%D0%A1%D0%BB%D1%83%D0%B6%D0%B5%D0%B1%D0%BD%D0%B0%D1%8F:%D0%98%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BE%D1%87%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%B8_%D0%BA%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%B3/9780700703142">ISBN 9780700703142</a>.</span><blockquote><p>Nizami was not a philosopher like Farabi, ibn Sina and Suhrawardi or the expositor of theoretical Sufism like Ibn 'Arabi and 'Abd al-Razzaq Kashani. However he should be regarded as philosopher and a gnostic who had who had mastered various fields of Islamic thought which he synthesized in a way to bring to mind the tradition of the Hakims who were to come after him such as Qutb al-Din Shirazi and Baba Afdal Kashani, who, while being masters of various school of knowledge, attempted to synthesize different traditions of philosophy, gnosis and theology.</p></blockquote></span>
</li>

Brill Academic Publishers. ISSN 1573-3912.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=bookitem&amp;rft.atitle=Ni%E1%BA%93%C4%81m%C4%AB+Gand%CC%B2j%CC%B2aw%C4%AB%2C+%E1%B8%8Ej%CC%B2amal+al-D%C4%ABn+Ab%C5%AB+Mu%E1%B8%A5ammad+Ily%C4%81s+b.+Y%C5%ABsuf+b.+Zak%C4%AB+Mu%CA%BEayyad&amp;rft.btitle=%D0%AD%D0%BD%D1%86%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%BB%D0%BE%D0%BF%D0%B5%D0%B4%D0%B8%D1%8F+%D0%B8%D1%81%D0%BB%D0%B0%D0%BC%D0%B0+Online&amp;rft.pub=Brill+Academic+Publishers&amp;rft.au=Chelkowski%2C+P.&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fru.wikipedia.org%3A%D0%9D%D0%B8%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BC%D0%B8+%D0%93%D1%8F%D0%BD%D0%B4%D0%B6%D0%B5%D0%B2%D0%B8"></span><span class="cs1-maint citation-comment"><code class="cs1-code">{{<a href="/wiki/%D0%A8%D0%B0%D0%B1%D0%BB%D0%BE%D0%BD:Cite_encyclopedia" title="Шаблон:Cite encyclopedia">cite encyclopedia</a>}}</code>:  Википедия:Обслуживание CS1 (множественные имена: editors list) (<a href="/wiki/%D0%9A%D0%B0%D1%82%D0%B5%D0%B3%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%B8%D1%8F:%D0%92%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%BF%D0%B5%D0%B4%D0%B8%D1%8F:%D0%9E%D0%B1%D1%81%D0%BB%D1%83%D0%B6%D0%B8%D0%B2%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%B5_CS1_(%D0%BC%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%B6%D0%B5%D1%81%D1%82%D0%B2%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%BD%D1%8B%D0%B5_%D0%B8%D0%BC%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B0:_editors_list)" title="Категория:Википедия:Обслуживание CS1 (множественные имена: editors list)">ссылка</a>)</span><blockquote><p>«Usually, there is more precise biographical information about the Persian court poets, but Nizāmī was not a court poet; he feared loss of integrity in this role and craved primarily for the freedom of artistic creation.»</p></blockquote></span>

<li id="cite_note-54"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-54">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text"><span class="citation"><i>K. A. Luther.</i> <span lang="en"><a class="external text" href="http://www.iranica.com/articles/atabakan-e-maraga-also-called-ahmadilis-a-family-of-local-rulers-of-maraga-who-ruled-from-the-early-6th-12th-cent" rel="nofollow">ATĀBAKĀN-E MARĀḠA</a></span> <span class="ref-info" style="cursor:help;" title="на английском языке">(англ.)</span>. Iranica (15 декабря 1987). Дата обращения: 2 сентября 2010. <a class="external text" href="https://www.webcitation.org/61HMIC6iR?url=http://www.iranicaonline.org/articles/atabakan-e-maraga-also-called-ahmadilis-a-family-of-local-rulers-of-maraga-who-ruled-from-the-early-6th-12th-cent" rel="nofollow">Архивировано</a> 28 августа 2011 года.</span><blockquote><p>«Alāʾ-al-dīn of Marāḡa… He seems to have been a man of pronounced literary interests, since at his request the poet Neẓāmī Ganǰavī composed the Haft peykar».</p></blockquote></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-55"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-55">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text"><span class="citation no-wikidata" data-wikidata-property-id="P1343"><i>Julie Scott Meisami.</i> <a class="external text" href="https://archive.org/details/haftpaykarmediev00niza" rel="nofollow">The Haft Paykar: A Medieval Persian Romance</a>. — Oxford University Press, 1995. — (Oxford World's Classics). — <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/%D0%A1%D0%BB%D1%83%D0%B6%D0%B5%D0%B1%D0%BD%D0%B0%D1%8F:%D0%98%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BE%D1%87%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%B8_%D0%BA%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%B3/0192831844">ISBN 0-19-283184-4</a>.</span><blockquote><p>«… Nizami was brought up by an uncle. <b>He was married three times</b>, and in his poems laments the death of each of his wives, as well as proferring advice to his son Muhammad. He lived in an age of both political instability and intense intellectual activity, which his poems reflect; but little is known about his life, his relations with his patrons, or the precise dates of his works, as the accounts of later biographers are colored by the many legends built up around the poet.»</p></blockquote></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-56"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-56">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text"><span class="citation"><i>Iraj Bashiri.</i> <span lang="und"><a class="external text" href="http://www.angelfire.com/rnb/bashiri/Teahouse/Figures.html#Nizami" rel="nofollow">The Teahouse at a Glance — Nizami’s Life and Works</a></span><span class="hidden-ref" style="display:none;">  <small class="ref-info" style="cursor:help;" title="на неопределённом языке">(неопр.)</small></span> (2000). Дата обращения: 6 сентября 2010. <a class="external text" href="https://www.webcitation.org/61HMIxMmR?url=http://www.angelfire.com/rnb/bashiri/Teahouse/Figures.html#Nizami" rel="nofollow">Архивировано</a> 28 августа 2011 года.</span></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-57"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-57">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text"><span class="citation no-wikidata" data-wikidata-property-id="P1343"><i>Julie Scott Meisami.</i> <a class="external text" href="https://archive.org/details/haftpaykarmediev00niza" rel="nofollow">The Haft Paykar: A Medieval Persian Romance</a>. — Oxford University Press, 1995. — (Oxford World's Classics). — <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/%D0%A1%D0%BB%D1%83%D0%B6%D0%B5%D0%B1%D0%BD%D0%B0%D1%8F:%D0%98%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BE%D1%87%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%B8_%D0%BA%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%B3/0192831844">ISBN 0-19-283184-4</a>.</span><blockquote><p>«… <b>He was married three times</b>, and <b>in his poems laments the death of each of his wives,</b> as well as proferring advice to his son Muhammad.»</p></blockquote></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-58"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-58">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text"><span class="citation no-wikidata" data-wikidata-property-id="P1343"><i>Julie Scott Meisami.</i> <a class="external text" href="https://archive.org/details/haftpaykarmediev00niza" rel="nofollow">The Haft Paykar: A Medieval Persian Romance</a>. — Oxford University Press, 1995. — (Oxford World's Classics). — <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/%D0%A1%D0%BB%D1%83%D0%B6%D0%B5%D0%B1%D0%BD%D0%B0%D1%8F:%D0%98%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BE%D1%87%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%B8_%D0%BA%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%B3/0192831844">ISBN 0-19-283184-4</a>.</span><blockquote><p>«… Nizami … <b>He lived in an age of both political instability and intense intellectual activity, which his poems reflect</b>; but little is known about his life, his relations with his patrons, or the precise dates of his works, as the accounts of later biographers are colored by the many legends built up around the poet.»</p></blockquote></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-59"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-59">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text"><span class="citation"><span lang="en"><a class="external text" href="http://persian.packhum.org/persian/main?url=pf%3Ffile%3D17604010%26ct%3D0" rel="nofollow">PREFACE</a></span> <span class="ref-info" style="cursor:help;" title="на английском языке">(англ.)</span>. <i>Lailî and Majnûn — Persian Literature in Translation</i>. The Packard Humanities Institute (2000). Дата обращения: 31 января 2011. <a class="external text" href="https://www.webcitation.org/61HMJTOZL?url=http://persian.packhum.org/persian/main?url=pf%3Ffile%3D17604010&amp;ct=0" rel="nofollow">Архивировано</a> 28 августа 2011 года.</span><blockquote><p>In honour of Nizámi, it is related that Ata Beg was desirous of forming and cultivating an acquaintance with him, and with that view ordered one of his courtiers to request his attendance. But it was replied, that Nizámi, being an austere recluse, studiously avoided all intercourse with princes. Ata Beg, on hearing this, and suspecting that the extreme piety and abstinence of Nizámi were affected, waited upon him in great pomp for the purpose of tempting and seducing him from his obscure retreat; but the result was highly favourable to the poet; and the prince ever afterwards looked upon him as a truly holy man, frequently visiting him, and treating him with the most profound respect and veneration. Nizámi also received many substantial proofs of the admiration in which his genius and learning were held. On one occasion, five thousand dinars were sent to him, and on another he was presented with an estate consisting of fourteen villages.</p></blockquote></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-60"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-60">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation encyclopaedia cs1" id="CITEREFChelkowski,_P.">Chelkowski, P. "Niẓāmī Gand̲j̲awī, Ḏj̲amal al-Dīn Abū Muḥammad Ilyās b. Yūsuf b. Zakī Muʾayyad". In P.J. Bearman, <a href="/wiki/%D0%91%D1%8C%D1%8F%D0%BD%D0%BA%D0%B8,_%D0%A2%D1%8C%D0%B5%D1%80%D1%80%D0%B8" title="Бьянки, Тьерри">Th. Bianquis</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/%D0%91%D0%BE%D1%81%D0%B2%D0%BE%D1%80%D1%82,_%D0%9A%D0%BB%D0%B8%D1%84%D1%84%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%B4_%D0%AD%D0%B4%D0%BC%D1%83%D0%BD%D0%B4" title="Босворт, Клиффорд Эдмунд">К. Эд. Босворт</a>, E. van Donzel and W.P. Heinrichs (ed.). <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Encyclopaedia_of_Islam" title="Encyclopaedia of Islam">Энциклопедия ислама Online</a></i>. Brill Academic Publishers. ISSN 1573-3912.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=bookitem&amp;rft.atitle=Ni%E1%BA%93%C4%81m%C4%AB+Gand%CC%B2j%CC%B2aw%C4%AB%2C+%E1%B8%8Ej%CC%B2amal+al-D%C4%ABn+Ab%C5%AB+Mu%E1%B8%A5ammad+Ily%C4%81s+b.+Y%C5%ABsuf+b.+Zak%C4%AB+Mu%CA%BEayyad&amp;rft.btitle=%D0%AD%D0%BD%D1%86%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%BB%D0%BE%D0%BF%D0%B5%D0%B4%D0%B8%D1%8F+%D0%B8%D1%81%D0%BB%D0%B0%D0%BC%D0%B0+Online&amp;rft.pub=Brill+Academic+Publishers&amp;rft.au=Chelkowski%2C+P.&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fru.wikipedia.org%3A%D0%9D%D0%B8%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BC%D0%B8+%D0%93%D1%8F%D0%BD%D0%B4%D0%B6%D0%B5%D0%B2%D0%B8"></span><span class="cs1-maint citation-comment"><code class="cs1-code">{{<a href="/wiki/%D0%A8%D0%B0%D0%B1%D0%BB%D0%BE%D0%BD:Cite_encyclopedia" title="Шаблон:Cite encyclopedia">cite encyclopedia</a>}}</code>:  Википедия:Обслуживание CS1 (множественные имена: editors list) (<a href="/wiki/%D0%9A%D0%B0%D1%82%D0%B5%D0%B3%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%B8%D1%8F:%D0%92%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%BF%D0%B5%D0%B4%D0%B8%D1%8F:%D0%9E%D0%B1%D1%81%D0%BB%D1%83%D0%B6%D0%B8%D0%B2%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%B5_CS1_(%D0%BC%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%B6%D0%B5%D1%81%D1%82%D0%B2%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%BD%D1%8B%D0%B5_%D0%B8%D0%BC%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B0:_editors_list)" title="Категория:Википедия:Обслуживание CS1 (множественные имена: editors list)">ссылка</a>)</span><blockquote><p>The traditional biographers, and some modern researchers, differ by six years about the exact date of his birth (535-40/1141-6), and as much as thirty-seven years about the date of his death (575—613/1180-1217). Now there is no doubt, however, that he died in the 7th/13th century, and the earlier dates must be discarded as erroneous.</p></blockquote></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-61"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-61">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text"><span class="citation no-wikidata" data-wikidata-property-id="P1343"><i>Francois De Blois.</i> <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=UeMOAAAAQAAJ&amp;dq=Persian+Literature+-+A+Bio+Bibliographical+Survey:+Volume+V+Poetry+of+the+Pre-Mongol+Period%22&amp;source=gbs_navlinks_s" rel="nofollow">Persian Literature — A Biobibliographical Survey: Volume V Poetry of the Pre-Mongol Period</a> / Francois De Blois. — Routledge, 2004. — Т. V. — С. 370. — 544 с. — <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/%D0%A1%D0%BB%D1%83%D0%B6%D0%B5%D0%B1%D0%BD%D0%B0%D1%8F:%D0%98%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BE%D1%87%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%B8_%D0%BA%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%B3/0947593470">ISBN 0947593470</a>. — <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/%D0%A1%D0%BB%D1%83%D0%B6%D0%B5%D0%B1%D0%BD%D0%B0%D1%8F:%D0%98%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BE%D1%87%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%B8_%D0%BA%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%B3/9780947593476">ISBN 9780947593476</a>.</span></span>

<li id="cite_note-62"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-62">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text"><span class="citation no-wikidata" data-wikidata-property-id="P1343"><i>Francois De Blois.</i> <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=UeMOAAAAQAAJ&amp;dq=Persian+Literature+-+A+Bio+Bibliographical+Survey:+Volume+V+Poetry+of+the+Pre-Mongol+Period%22&amp;source=gbs_navlinks_s" rel="nofollow">Persian Literature — A Biobibliographical Survey: Volume V Poetry of the Pre-Mongol Period</a> / Francois De Blois. — Routledge, 2004. — Т. V. — С. 369. — 544 с. — <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/%D0%A1%D0%BB%D1%83%D0%B6%D0%B5%D0%B1%D0%BD%D0%B0%D1%8F:%D0%98%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BE%D1%87%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%B8_%D0%BA%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%B3/0947593470">ISBN 0947593470</a>. — <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/%D0%A1%D0%BB%D1%83%D0%B6%D0%B5%D0%B1%D0%BD%D0%B0%D1%8F:%D0%98%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BE%D1%87%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%B8_%D0%BA%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%B3/9780947593476">ISBN 9780947593476</a>.</span></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-63"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-63">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text">Низами Гянджеви. Собрание сочинений в 3 т. Т. 3. С. 688. — Баку: «Азернешр», 1991</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-64"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-64">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text"><span class="citation no-wikidata" data-wikidata-property-id="P1343"><i>Peter J. Chelkowski.</i> <a class="external text" href="https://archive.org/details/mirrorofinvisibl0000chel" rel="nofollow">Mirror of the Invisible World</a>. — New York: Metropolitan Museum of Art, 1975. — С. <a class="external text" href="https://archive.org/details/mirrorofinvisibl0000chel/page/1" rel="nofollow">1</a>.</span><blockquote><p>The culture of Nizami’s Persia is renowned for its deep-rooted tradition and splendor. In pre-Islamic times, it had developed extraordinarily rich and exact means of expression in music, architecture, and daily life as well as in writing, although Iran, its center--or, as the poets believed, its heart--was continually overrun by invading armies and immigrants, this tradition was able to absorb, transform, and ultimately overcome foreign intrusion. Alexander the Great was only one of many conquerors, to be seduced by the Persian way of life.</p></blockquote></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-65"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-65">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text"><span class="citation no-wikidata" data-wikidata-property-id="P1343"><i>Peter J. Chelkowski.</i> Nezami's Iskandarnameh, Colloquio sul poeta persiano Nizami e la leggenda iranica di Alessandro magno. — Roma, 1977. — С. 13.</span><blockquote><p>Nizami was a typical product of the Iranian culture. He created a bridge between Islamic Iran and pre-Islamic Iran and also between Iran and the whole ancient world.</p></blockquote></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-66"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-66">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text"><span class="citation no-wikidata" data-wikidata-property-id="P1343"><i>Jan Rypka.</i> <a class="external text" href="https://archive.org/details/historyiranianli00rypk" rel="nofollow">History of Iranian literature (перевод «Dějiny perské a tadžické literatury», Praha: ČSAV, 1956)</a> / Karl Jahn. — Netherlands: Reidel Publishing Company, 1968. — С. <a class="external text" href="https://archive.org/details/historyiranianli00rypk/page/n107" rel="nofollow">76</a>. — 929 с. — <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/%D0%A1%D0%BB%D1%83%D0%B6%D0%B5%D0%B1%D0%BD%D0%B0%D1%8F:%D0%98%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BE%D1%87%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%B8_%D0%BA%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%B3/9027701431">ISBN 9027701431</a>.</span><blockquote><p>The centripetal tendency is evident in the unity of Persian literature from the points of view of language and content and also in the sense of civic unity. Even the Caucasian Nizami, although living on the far-flung periphery, does not manifest a different spirit and apostrophizes Iran as the Heart of the World.</p></blockquote></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-67"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-67">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text"><span class="citation no-wikidata" data-wikidata-property-id="P1343"><i>Pepe Escobar.</i> Globalistan: How the Globalized World is Dissolving into Liquid War. — Nimble Books, 2007. — С. 10. — 368 с. — <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/%D0%A1%D0%BB%D1%83%D0%B6%D0%B5%D0%B1%D0%BD%D0%B0%D1%8F:%D0%98%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BE%D1%87%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%B8_%D0%BA%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%B3/0978813820">ISBN 0978813820</a>, 9780978813826.</span><blockquote><p>… the great 12th century Persian poet Nezami, who in the famous Haft Peykar («The Seven Portraits») wrote that «The world is the body and Iran is its heart».</p></blockquote></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-68"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-68">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text"><span class="citation"><i>نظامی گنجوی.</i> <span lang="fa"><a class="external text" href="http://ganjoor.net/nezami/5ganj/7peykar/sh5/" rel="nofollow">هفت پیکر</a></span> <span class="ref-info" style="cursor:help;" title="на персидском языке">(перс.)</span>. <i>آثار سخنسرایان پارسی‌گو</i>. Дата обращения: 10 февраля 2011. <a class="external text" href="https://www.webcitation.org/61HMJxk6I?url=http://ganjoor.net/hafez/montasab/sh5/" rel="nofollow">Архивировано</a> 28 августа 2011 года.</span><blockquote><p>چونکه ایران دل زمین باشد:
</p></blockquote><blockquote>
<blockquote class="ts-Начало_цитаты-quote">
<p class="mw-empty-elt">
</p>
<dl><dd>Весь мир — тело, а Иран — сердце,</dd>
<dd>Не устыдится высказавший это сравнение.</dd>
<dd>Так как Иран — сердце мира,</dd>
<dd>то сердце лучше тела, несомненно.</dd>
<dd><i>(подстрочный перевод с персидского)</i></dd></dl>
<div class="mw-collapsible mw-collapsed has-collapsible-header ts-Скрытый_блок ts-Скрытый_блок-gray ts-Скрытый_блок-noneHideLink ts-oq has-collapsible-header" style=""><div class="ts-Скрытый_блок-title collapsible-header ts-Скрытый_блок-title-leftTitle ts-oq-header collapsible-header" style="text-align:left;">Оригинальный текст <small class="ref-info" style="cursor:help;" title="на персидском языке">(перс.)</small></div><div class="mw-collapsible-content ts-oq-content" style="">
<div dir="auto" lang="fa">همه عالم تن است و ایران دل
<dl><dd>نیست گوینده زین قیاس خجل</dd>
<dd>چونکه ایران دل زمین باشد</dd>
<dd>دل ز تن به بود یقین باشد</dd></dl>
</div>
</div></div></blockquote>
</blockquote></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-69"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-69">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text"><span class="citation no-wikidata" data-wikidata-property-id="P1343"><i>Nizami Ganjavi.</i> <a class="external text" href="https://www.amazon.com/Haft-Paykar-Medieval-Persian-Classics/dp/0192831844/ref=sr_1_1?s=books&amp;ie=UTF8&amp;qid=1286217678&amp;sr=1-1" rel="nofollow">Haft Paykar: A Medieval Persian Romance</a> <small class="ref-info" style="cursor:help;" title="на английском языке">(англ.)</small> / J. S. Meisami (Editor). — USA: Oxford University Press, 1995. — P. 19. — 368 p. — <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/%D0%A1%D0%BB%D1%83%D0%B6%D0%B5%D0%B1%D0%BD%D0%B0%D1%8F:%D0%98%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BE%D1%87%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%B8_%D0%BA%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%B3/9780192831842">ISBN 978-0192831842</a>. <small><a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20230326215932/https://www.amazon.com/Haft-Paykar-Medieval-Persian-Classics/dp/0192831844/ref=sr_1_1?s=books&amp;ie=UTF8&amp;qid=1286217678&amp;sr=1-1" rel="nofollow">Архивировано</a> 26 марта 2023 года.</small></span><blockquote><p>The world is a body, Iran its heart,
</p><dl><dd>No shame to him who says such a word</dd>
<dd>Iran, the world’s most precious heart,</dd>
<dd>excels the body, there is no doubt.</dd>
<dd>Among the realms the kings posses,</dd>
<dd>the best domain goes to the best.</dd></dl>
</blockquote></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-70"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-70">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text"><span class="citation"><i>NIZĀMĪ OF GANJA (Editor and translator - C. E. Wilson).</i> <span lang="en"><a class="external text" href="https://www.webcitation.org/61HMKWFN9?url=http://persian.packhum.org/persian/main?url=pf%3Ffile%3D17601040&amp;ct=11" rel="nofollow">THE HAFT PAIKAR (THE SEVEN BEAUTIES)</a></span> <span class="ref-info" style="cursor:help;" title="на английском языке">(англ.)</span>. <i>Persian Literature in Translation</i>. The Packard Humanities Institute (1924(London)). Дата обращения: 4 октября 2010. Архивировано из <a class="external text" href="http://persian.packhum.org/persian/main?url=pf%3Ffile%3D17601040%26ct%3D11" rel="nofollow">оригинала</a> 28 августа 2011 года.</span><blockquote><p>The world entire is body, Persia, heart,
</p><dl><dd>the writer shames not at this parallel;</dd>
<dd>For since that land’s the heart of (all) the earth</dd>
<dd>the heart is better than the body, sure*295.</dd>
<dd>Of these dominions which the rulers have</dd>
<dd>the best of places to the best accrue.</dd></dl></blockquote> Сноска: <blockquote><p>295. <b>The sense is apparently, «since Persia is the heart of the earth, Persia is the best part of the earth, because it is certain that the heart is better than the body.</b>»</p></blockquote></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-71"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-71">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text">«Семь красавиц», пер. В. Державина. Низами. Собр. соч. В 3-х т. Баку, 1991. Т.2. С. 324</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-72"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-72">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text"><span class="citation no-wikidata" data-wikidata-property-id="P1343"><i>Chelkowski, P.</i> "Nezami's Iskandarnameh:"in Colloquio sul poeta persiano Nizami e la leggenda iranica di Alessandro magno. — Roma, 1977.</span><blockquote><p>«It seems that Nezami’s favorite pastime was reading Firdawsi’s monumental epic Shahnameh(The book of Kings)»</p></blockquote></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-73"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-73">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text"><span class="citation no-wikidata" data-wikidata-property-id="P1343"><i>Chelkowski, P.</i> "Nezami's Iskandarnameh:"in Colloquio sul poeta persiano Nizami e la leggenda iranica di Alessandro magno. — Roma, 1977.</span><blockquote><p>«However, it was not Tabari directly, but Ferdowsi who was Nizami’s source of inspiration and material in composing Iskandarnameh. Nizami constantly alludes to the Shahnameh in his writing, especially in the prologue to the Iskandarnameh. It seems that he was always fascinated by the work of Firdawsi and made it a goal of his life to write an heroic epic of the same stature.»</p></blockquote></span>
</li>

<li id="cite_note-75"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-75">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text"><span class="citation no-wikidata" data-wikidata-property-id="P1343"><i>Бертэльс, Е. Э.</i> "Низами и Фирдоуси". — Баку, 1981.</span></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-76"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-76">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text"><span class="citation"><i>Dick Davis.</i> <span lang="en"><a class="external text" href="http://www.iranica.com/articles/vis-o-ramin" rel="nofollow">VIS O RĀMIN</a></span> <span class="ref-info" style="cursor:help;" title="на английском языке">(англ.)</span>. Iranica (20 июля 2005). Дата обращения: 4 сентября 2010. <a class="external text" href="https://www.webcitation.org/61HML4TpV?url=http://www.iranicaonline.org/articles/vis-o-ramin" rel="nofollow">Архивировано</a> 28 августа 2011 года.</span><blockquote><p>The poem had an immense influence on Neẓāmi, who takes the bases for most of his plots from Ferdowsi but the basis for his rhetoric from Gorgāni. This is especially noticeable in his Ḵosrow o Širin, which imitates a major scene (that of the lovers arguing in the snow) from Vis o Rāmin, as well as being in the same meter (hazaj) as Gorgāni’s poem. Nezami’s concern with astrology also has a precedent in an elaborate astrological description of the night sky in Vis o Rāmin. Given Nezami’s own paramount influence on the romance tradition, Gorgāni can be said to have initiated much of the distinctive rhetoric and poetic atmosphere of this tradition, with the exception of its Sufi preoccupations, which are quite absent from his poem.</p></blockquote></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-77"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-77">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text"><span class="citation"><i>J.T.P. De Bruijn.</i> <span lang="en"><a class="external text" href="http://www.iranica.com/articles/hadiqat-al-haqiqa-wasariat-al-tariqa" rel="nofollow">ḤADIQAT AL-ḤAQIQA WA ŠARIʿAT AL-ṬARIQA</a></span> <span class="ref-info" style="cursor:help;" title="на английском языке">(англ.)</span>. Iranica (15 декабря 2002). Дата обращения: 6 сентября 2010. <a class="external text" href="https://www.webcitation.org/61HMLrrhP?url=http://www.iranicaonline.org/articles/hadiqat-al-haqiqa-wasariat-al-tariqa" rel="nofollow">Архивировано</a> 28 августа 2011 года.</span><blockquote><p>The Ḥadiqat al-ḥaqiqa is not only one of the first of a long line of Persian didactical maṯnawis, it is also one of the most popular works of its kind as the great number of copies made throughout the centuries attest. Its great impact on Persian literature is evidenced by the numerous citations from the poem occurring in mystical as well as profane works. It has been taken as a model by several other poets, including Neẓāmi, ʿAṭṭār, Rumi, Awḥadi, and Jāmi.</p></blockquote></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-78"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-78">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text">JTP de Bruijn. Persian Sufi Poetry, An Introduction to the Mystical — Taylor and Francis(Routledge) 1997 pp 97:<blockquote><p>The first poet who frankly acknowledged his indebtedness to Sanai as a writer of a didactical Masnavi was Ilyas ibn Yusuf Nizami of Ganja (1141—1209).</p></blockquote></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-79"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-79">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation encyclopaedia cs1" id="CITEREFChelkowski,_P.">Chelkowski, P. Эд. Босворт</a>, E. van Donzel and W.P. Heinrichs (ed.). <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Encyclopaedia_of_Islam" title="Encyclopaedia of Islam">Энциклопедия ислама Online</a></i>. The plot in his romantic stories is carefully constructed to enhance the stories' psychological complexities. The characters work and grow under the stress of action to discover things about themselves and others and to make swift decisions.</p></blockquote></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-80"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-80">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation encyclopaedia cs1" id="CITEREFChelkowski,_P.">Chelkowski, P. </li>
<li id="cite_note-81"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-81">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation encyclopaedia cs1" id="CITEREFChelkowski,_P.">Chelkowski, P. Artisans were particularly dear to him. Painters, sculptors, architects and musicians are carefully portrayed and often play crucial roles.</p></blockquote></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-82"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-82">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation encyclopaedia cs1" id="CITEREFChelkowski,_P.">Chelkowski, P. In erotic sensuous verse, he explains what makes human beings behave as they do, revealing their follies and their glories, all their struggles, unbridled passions and tragedies.</p></blockquote></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-83"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-83">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation encyclopaedia cs1" id="CITEREFChelkowski,_P.">Chelkowski, P. Bianquis, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/%D0%91%D0%BE%D1%81%D0%B2%D0%BE%D1%80%D1%82,_%D0%9A%D0%BB%D0%B8%D1%84%D1%84%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%B4_%D0%AD%D0%B4%D0%BC%D1%83%D0%BD%D0%B4" title="Босворт, Клиффорд Эдмунд">К. Эд. Босворт</a>, E. van Donzel and W.P. Heinrichs (ed.). <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Encyclopaedia_of_Islam" title="Encyclopaedia of Islam">Энциклопедия ислама Online</a></i>. Brill Academic Publishers. ISSN 1573-3912.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=bookitem&amp;rft.atitle=Ni%E1%BA%93%C4%81m%C4%AB+Gand%CC%B2j%CC%B2aw%C4%AB%2C+%E1%B8%8Ej%CC%B2amal+al-D%C4%ABn+Ab%C5%AB+Mu%E1%B8%A5ammad+Ily%C4%81s+b.+Y%C5%ABsuf+b.+Zak%C4%AB+Mu%CA%BEayyad&amp;rft.btitle=%D0%AD%D0%BD%D1%86%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%BB%D0%BE%D0%BF%D0%B5%D0%B4%D0%B8%D1%8F+%D0%B8%D1%81%D0%BB%D0%B0%D0%BC%D0%B0+Online&amp;rft.pub=Brill+Academic+Publishers&amp;rft.au=Chelkowski%2C+P.&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fru.wikipedia.org%3A%D0%9D%D0%B8%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BC%D0%B8+%D0%93%D1%8F%D0%BD%D0%B4%D0%B6%D0%B5%D0%B2%D0%B8"></span><span class="cs1-maint citation-comment"><code class="cs1-code">{{<a href="/wiki/%D0%A8%D0%B0%D0%B1%D0%BB%D0%BE%D0%BD:Cite_encyclopedia" title="Шаблон:Cite encyclopedia">cite encyclopedia</a>}}</code>:  Википедия:Обслуживание CS1 (множественные имена: editors list) (<a href="/wiki/%D0%9A%D0%B0%D1%82%D0%B5%D0%B3%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%B8%D1%8F:%D0%92%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%BF%D0%B5%D0%B4%D0%B8%D1%8F:%D0%9E%D0%B1%D1%81%D0%BB%D1%83%D0%B6%D0%B8%D0%B2%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%B5_CS1_(%D0%BC%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%B6%D0%B5%D1%81%D1%82%D0%B2%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%BD%D1%8B%D0%B5_%D0%B8%D0%BC%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B0:_editors_list)" title="Категория:Википедия:Обслуживание CS1 (множественные имена: editors list)">ссылка</a>)</span><blockquote><p>To Niẓāmī, truth was the very essence of poetry. On this principle, he attacks the court poets who sell their integrity and talents for earthly returns. The Islamic law served as the loom on which the philosophy of his Mak̲h̲zan al-asrār was woven in intricate patterns. He was looking for universal justice, and is trying to protect the poor and humble people and to put under scrutiny the excesses of the powerful of the world. The guidelines for people in the poem are accompanied by warnings of the transitory nature of life.</p></blockquote></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-84"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-84">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text"><span class="citation no-wikidata" data-wikidata-property-id="P1343"><i>Abdolhossein Zarrinkoob.</i> <span data-wikidata-qualifier-id="P248">Nizami, a life-long quest for a utopia</span> // Colloquio sul poeta persiano Nizami e la leggenda iranica di Alessandro magno (ROMA, 25-26 MARZO 1975) / G. Bardi. — Roma: deH'Accademia Nazionale dei Lincei, 1977. — P. 5.</span><blockquote><p>… the poet Nizami has attempted to picture a perfect society—a utopia.</p></blockquote></span>
</li>

<li id="cite_note-91"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-91">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text"><span class="citation no-wikidata" data-wikidata-property-id="P1343"><i>Subtelny, Maria.</i> <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=dmclFThar_UC&amp;source=gbs_navlinks_s" rel="nofollow">Visionary Rose: Metaphorical Application of Horticultural Practice in Persian Culture, «Botanical progress, horticultural information and cultural changes»</a> / Michel Conan and W. Even the advent of Islam to Iran did not exert a negative impact on Persian garden culture.</p></blockquote></span>

<li id="cite_note-100"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-100">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text"><span class="citation no-wikidata" data-wikidata-property-id="P1343"><i>Subtelny, Maria.</i> <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=dmclFThar_UC&amp;source=gbs_navlinks_s" rel="nofollow">Visionary Rose: Metaphorical Application of Horticultural Practice in Persian Culture, «Botanical progress, horticultural information and cultural changes»</a> / Michel Conan and W. John Kress. — USA: Dumbarton Oaks, 2007. — Т. 2004. — С. 19. — 278 с. — <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/%D0%A1%D0%BB%D1%83%D0%B6%D0%B5%D0%B1%D0%BD%D0%B0%D1%8F:%D0%98%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BE%D1%87%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%B8_%D0%BA%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%B3/0884023273">ISBN 0884023273</a>, 9780884023272.</span><blockquote><p>Although the tale points primarily to the power of psychological suggestion, what is of significance for our topic is that it is the mysterious nature of scent, and of the scent of the rose in particular, that serves as the metaphorical vehicle in this classic text of medival Persian poetic narrative.</p></blockquote></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-101"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-101">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text"><span class="citation no-wikidata" data-wikidata-property-id="P1343"><i>Низами Гянджеви.</i> Семь красавиц / перевод Вл. Державина. — <abbr title="Москва">М.</abbr>: ГИХЛ, 1959. — 396 с.</span></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-102"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-102">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation encyclopaedia cs1" id="CITEREFChelkowski,_P.">Chelkowski, P. Bianquis, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/%D0%91%D0%BE%D1%81%D0%B2%D0%BE%D1%80%D1%82,_%D0%9A%D0%BB%D0%B8%D1%84%D1%84%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%B4_%D0%AD%D0%B4%D0%BC%D1%83%D0%BD%D0%B4" title="Босворт, Клиффорд Эдмунд">К. Эд. Босворт</a>, E. van Donzel and W.P. Heinrichs (ed.). <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Encyclopaedia_of_Islam" title="Encyclopaedia of Islam">Энциклопедия ислама Online</a></i>. Brill Academic Publishers. ISSN 1573-3912.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=bookitem&amp;rft.atitle=Ni%E1%BA%93%C4%81m%C4%AB+Gand%CC%B2j%CC%B2aw%C4%AB%2C+%E1%B8%8Ej%CC%B2amal+al-D%C4%ABn+Ab%C5%AB+Mu%E1%B8%A5ammad+Ily%C4%81s+b.+Y%C5%ABsuf+b.+Zak%C4%AB+Mu%CA%BEayyad&amp;rft.btitle=%D0%AD%D0%BD%D1%86%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%BB%D0%BE%D0%BF%D0%B5%D0%B4%D0%B8%D1%8F+%D0%B8%D1%81%D0%BB%D0%B0%D0%BC%D0%B0+Online&amp;rft.pub=Brill+Academic+Publishers&amp;rft.au=Chelkowski%2C+P.&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fru.wikipedia.org%3A%D0%9D%D0%B8%D0%B7%D0%B0%D0%BC%D0%B8+%D0%93%D1%8F%D0%BD%D0%B4%D0%B6%D0%B5%D0%B2%D0%B8"></span><span class="cs1-maint citation-comment"><code class="cs1-code">{{<a href="/wiki/%D0%A8%D0%B0%D0%B1%D0%BB%D0%BE%D0%BD:Cite_encyclopedia" title="Шаблон:Cite encyclopedia">cite encyclopedia</a>}}</code>:  Википедия:Обслуживание CS1 (множественные имена: editors list) (<a href="/wiki/%D0%9A%D0%B0%D1%82%D0%B5%D0%B3%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%B8%D1%8F:%D0%92%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%BF%D0%B5%D0%B4%D0%B8%D1%8F:%D0%9E%D0%B1%D1%81%D0%BB%D1%83%D0%B6%D0%B8%D0%B2%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%B5_CS1_(%D0%BC%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%B6%D0%B5%D1%81%D1%82%D0%B2%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%BD%D1%8B%D0%B5_%D0%B8%D0%BC%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%B0:_editors_list)" title="Категория:Википедия:Обслуживание CS1 (множественные имена: editors list)">ссылка</a>)</span><blockquote><p>In Islamic cosmology, the earth was placed in the centre of the seven planets: the moon, Mercury, Venus, the sun, Mars, Jupiter and Saturn. These were considered agents of God, and in their motion influenced beings and events on earth. Niẓāmī firmly believed as well that the unity of the world could be perceived through arithmetical, geometrical, and musical relations. Numbers were the key to the one interconnected universe; for through numbers multiplicity becomes unity and discordance, harmony.</p></blockquote></span>
</li>

He introduces new and lucid metaphors and images as well as coining new words.</p></blockquote></span>

<li id="cite_note-106"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-106">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text"><span class="citation no-wikidata" data-wikidata-property-id="P1343"><i>A. A. <li id="cite_note-107"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-107">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text"><span class="citation no-wikidata" data-wikidata-property-id="P1343"><i>A. A. <li id="cite_note-108"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-108">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text"><span class="citation no-wikidata" data-wikidata-property-id="P1343"><i>A. A. Brill, 2003. — С. 34. — 395 с. — <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/%D0%A1%D0%BB%D1%83%D0%B6%D0%B5%D0%B1%D0%BD%D0%B0%D1%8F:%D0%98%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BE%D1%87%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%B8_%D0%BA%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%B3/9004129421">ISBN 9004129421</a>.</span><blockquote><p>Another salient feature of Nizamfs style is the introduction of aphorisms. Long passages of Layll and Majnun are composed in epigrammatic style, and many of the poem’s maxims have become proverbs.</p></blockquote></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-109"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-109">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text"><span class="citation no-wikidata" data-wikidata-property-id="P1343"><i>A. A. Seyed-Gohrab.</i> Layli and Majnun: Love, Madness and Mystic Longing in Nezāmi’s Epic Romance. — Leiden / Boston: E.J. Brill, 2003. — С. 33. — 395 с. — <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/%D0%A1%D0%BB%D1%83%D0%B6%D0%B5%D0%B1%D0%BD%D0%B0%D1%8F:%D0%98%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BE%D1%87%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%B8_%D0%BA%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%B3/9004129421">ISBN 9004129421</a>.</span><blockquote><p>… the use of concise and pithy expressions but also in the insertion of colloquial speech. The poet’s language is idiomatically rich but stylistically deceptively relaxed and simple, especially in dialogues and monologues.</p></blockquote></span>

<li id="cite_note-110"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-110">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text"><span class="citation no-wikidata" data-wikidata-property-id="P1343"><i>A. A. Brill, 2003. — С. 31. — 395 с. — <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/%D0%A1%D0%BB%D1%83%D0%B6%D0%B5%D0%B1%D0%BD%D0%B0%D1%8F:%D0%98%D1%81%D1%82%D0%BE%D1%87%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%B8_%D0%BA%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%B3/9004129421">ISBN 9004129421</a>.</span><blockquote><p>Nizami describes his own style as gharib, meaning 'rare,' 'unique,' 'strange,' or nau, 'new,' 'novel.' He refers to himself as the magician of words whose name is "the mirror of the invisible.</p></blockquote></span>

<li id="cite_note-112"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-112">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text"><span class="citation"><i>Moḥammad Amin Riāḥi.</i> <span lang="en"><a class="external text" href="http://www.iranica.com/articles/nozhat-al-majales" rel="nofollow">NOZHAT AL-MAJĀLES</a></span> <span class="ref-info" style="cursor:help;" title="на английском языке">(англ.)</span>. <a href="/wiki/Encyclop%C3%A6dia_Iranica" title="Encyclopædia Iranica">Encyclopædia Iranica</a> (15 декабря 2008). Цифровая версия <a class="external autonumber" href="https://tarnama.org/library/Nozhat.al-Majales.pdf" rel="nofollow">[1]</a> <a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20101130111133/https://tarnama.org/library/Nozhat.al-Majales.pdf" rel="nofollow">Архивная копия</a> от 30 ноября 2010 на <a href="/wiki/Wayback_Machine" title="Wayback Machine">Wayback Machine</a><a class="external autonumber" href="http://www.azargoshnasp.net/Pasokhbehanirani/Nozhat_al_Majales.pdf" rel="nofollow">[2]</a></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-114"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-114">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text"><span class="citation"><i>Paola Orsatti.</i> <span lang="en"><a class="external text" href="http://www.iranica.com/articles/kosrow-o-sirin" rel="nofollow">ḴOSROW O ŠIRIN</a></span> <span class="ref-info" style="cursor:help;" title="на английском языке">(англ.)</span>. Iranica (15 августа 2006). Дата обращения: 16 сентября 2010. <a class="external text" href="https://www.webcitation.org/61HMNSYm6?url=http://www.iranicaonline.org/articles/kosrow-o-sirin" rel="nofollow">Архивировано</a> 28 августа 2011 года.</span><blockquote><p>Ḵosrow o Širin… The poem was composed over a period of about 16 lunar years, between 571/1175-6 and 587/1191 (cf. de Blois, pp. 440, 446; Zarrinkub, p. 25ff.). It contains eulogies to the Seljuq sultan Ṭöḡrol III b. Arsalān (571 /1175-6-590/1194), to his nominal vassal but actual master, the atābak (q.v.) of Azerbaijan Abu Jaʿfar Moḥammad b. Ildegez Jahān-Pahlavān (571/1175-6-582/1186-7), and to the latter’s brother and successor Qezel Arsalān (582/1186-7 to 587/1191).</p></blockquote></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-Chelkowski,_P-115"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">↑ <a href="#cite_ref-Chelkowski,_P_115-0"><sup><i><b>1</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Chelkowski,_P_115-1"><sup><i><b>2</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation encyclopaedia cs1" id="CITEREFChelkowski,_P.">Chelkowski, P. Bianquis, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/%D0%91%D0%BE%D1%81%D0%B2%D0%BE%D1%80%D1%82,_%D0%9A%D0%BB%D0%B8%D1%84%D1%84%D0%BE%D1%80%D0%B4_%D0%AD%D0%B4%D0%BC%D1%83%D0%BD%D0%B4" title="Босворт, Клиффорд Эдмунд">К. <li id="cite_note-116"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-116">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text"><span class="citation"><i>François de Blois.</i> <span lang="en"><a class="external text" href="http://www.iranica.com/articles/haft-peykar" rel="nofollow">HAFT PEYKAR</a></span> <span class="ref-info" style="cursor:help;" title="на английском языке">(англ.)</span>. Iranica (15 декабря 2002). Дата обращения: 9 февраля 2011. <a class="external text" href="https://www.webcitation.org/61HMOCiCa?url=http://www.iranicaonline.org/articles/haft-peykar" rel="nofollow">Архивировано</a> 28 августа 2011 года.</span><blockquote><p>But the manuscripts of the ‘a’ recension have altered (or miscopied?) the name of the dedicatee to Qïzïl Arslān, retained the verse giving the day, month and hour of completion, but altered the year to «after ṯā (variant: tā) and ṣād and ḥē» i.e., either «after 498» (which is much too early) or «after 598/1202.»</p></blockquote></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-117"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-117">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text"><span class="citation"><i>François de Blois.</i> <span lang="en"><a class="external text" href="http://www.iranica.com/articles/eskandar-nama-of-nezami" rel="nofollow">ESKANDAR-NĀMA OF NEŻĀMĪ</a></span> <span class="ref-info" style="cursor:help;" title="на английском языке">(англ.)</span>. Iranica (15 декабря 1998). Дата обращения: 9 февраля 2011. <a class="external text" href="https://www.webcitation.org/61HMOxGr5?url=http://www.iranicaonline.org/articles/eskandar-nama-of-nezami" rel="nofollow">Архивировано</a> 28 августа 2011 года.</span><blockquote><p>This suggests that Neẓāmī originally planned to dedicate the Eskandar-nāma, like Leylī o Majnūn, to one of the kings of Šarvān. But that dynasty evidently lost power over Ganja by the time the poems were completed, and <b>in their final form they are dedicated to the malek of Ahar, Noṣrat-al-Dīn Bīškīn b. Moḥammad.</b> This ruler is mentioned in the introduction to Šaraf-nāma, chap. 10, vv. 11-12, where the poet makes a pun on his name Bīškīn («whose hatred is more»), though some of the manuscripts have a superscription claiming (wrongly) that the verses evoke Bīškīn’s overlord, the atabeg Noṣrat-al-Dīn Abū Bakr.</p></blockquote></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-118"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-118">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation encyclopaedia cs1" id="CITEREFChelkowski,_P.">Chelkowski, P. </li>
<li id="cite_note-119"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-119">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text"><span class="citation"><i>Domenico Parrello.</i> <span lang="en"><a class="external text" href="http://www.iranica.com/articles/kamsa-of-nezami" rel="nofollow">ḴAMSA OF NEẒĀMI</a></span> <span class="ref-info" style="cursor:help;" title="на английском языке">(англ.)</span>. Encyclopædia Iranica (10 ноября 2010). Дата обращения: 5 февраля 2011. <a class="external text" href="https://www.webcitation.org/61HMPhiDF?url=http://www.iranicaonline.org/articles/kamsa-of-nezami" rel="nofollow">Архивировано</a> 28 августа 2011 года.</span><blockquote><p>It contains the didactic poem Maḵzan al-asrār in around 2,260 couplets in sariʿ meter; three epic romances: Ḵosrow o Širin (q.v.) in around 6,500 couplets in hazaj meter, Leyli o Majnun (q.v.) in around 4,600 couplets in hazaj meter, and Haft peykar (q.v.) in about 5130 couplets in ḵafif meter; and the Eskandar-nāma (q.v.), which can be regarded as an epic interlaced with didactic observations and consists of two formally separate parts, in all about 10,500 couplets in motaqāreb meter.</p></blockquote></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-120"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-120">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text"><span class="citation"><i>A. A. <li id="cite_note-IranicaClassical-122"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-IranicaClassical_122-0">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text"><span class="citation"><i>CHARLES-HENRI DE FOUCHÉCOUR.</i> <span lang="en"><a class="external text" href="http://www.iranica.com/articles/iran-viii2-classical-persian-literature" rel="nofollow">IRAN:Classical Persian Literature</a></span> <span class="ref-info" style="cursor:help;" title="на английском языке">(англ.)</span>. <li id="cite_note-123"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-123">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text"><span class="citation no-wikidata" data-wikidata-property-id="P1343"><i>Peter J. <li id="cite_note-124"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-124">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text"><span class="citation no-wikidata" data-wikidata-property-id="P1343"><i>Peter J. <li id="cite_note-126"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><a href="#cite_ref-126">↑</a></span> <span class="reference-text"><span class="citation"><i>Paola Orsatti.</i> <span lang="en"><a class="external text" href="http://www.iranica.com/articles/kosrow-o-sirin" rel="nofollow">ḴOSROW O ŠIRIN</a></span> <span class="ref-info" style="cursor:help;" title="на английском языке">(англ.)</span>. Iranica (15 августа 2006). Дата обращения: 16 сентября 2010. <a class="external text" href="https://www.webcitation.org/61HMNSYm6?url=http://www.iranicaonline.org/articles/kosrow-o-sirin" rel="nofollow">Архивировано</a> 28 августа 2011 года.</span><blockquote><p>… the perusal of Gorgāni’s Vis o Rāmin, inspired Neẓāmi’s second major narrative poem: Ḵosrow and Širin (1181), his first masterpiece.</p></blockquote></span>
